<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">A small and flexible metal mountable UHF RFID tag antenna, utilizing a high-permittivity substrate material is presented. The tag is composed of a small single-layer T-matched dipole antenna, on a flexible ceramic (BaTiO<sub>3</sub>) polymer (polydimethylsiloxane) composite substrate, with a thickness of 1.5 mm. The flexibility of the substrate allows it to be mounted on flat and cylindrical metallic surfaces. The performance of the developed tag is evaluated through simulations and measurements on both flat and cylindrical metallic platforms of various sizes. The results show that the tag achieves state-of-the-art size-performance ratio while meeting the key requirements of an affordable RFID tag with a simple and flexible structure.</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>There has been an increasing need and rapid progress in the field of wireless identification and communications. Radio frequency identification (RFID) is gaining great attention to wirelessly track and identify objects in an effective and reliable manner. An RFID system is composed of two main components, the reader and the tag. The passive RFID tag usually is composed of a tag antenna and an IC chip. The tag IC contains an identification code (ID) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a> activated by an incident continuous wave from the reader antenna. Once activated, the tag IC listens in for commands from the reader and modulates the scattering of the incident field accordingly <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. The input impedance and reflectivity of a tag antenna rely on the electromagnetic properties of the substrate or material to which it is attached and on the geometry of the antenna. Using a substrate with a higher permittivity value can be useful in reducing the overall size of the tag antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>.</p><p>Substrates play a major role in the development of radio frequency electronics and antenna designs. Similarly, there has been a growing interest in recent years to develop flexible antennas and RFID tags. Fabricating a flexible electronics substrate also brings the challenge to achieve a material that is low-loss and less vulnerable to heat, water, and other damaging effects.</p><p>An antenna at a distance much less than a quarter wavelength from a conductive surface, the electromagnetic fields radiated by the image current, and the antenna sum up with approximately 180° phase difference and cancel each other largely. This will affect the input impedance, resonance frequency, gain, radiation pattern, and the efficiency of the tag antenna. Therefore, designing a metal mountable tag antenna is challenging. Several on-metal tag antennas have been proposed in recent years, utilizing various techniques to reduce the effects of the metallic back plane. Some of these techniques include designing patch-style antennas, using high-dielectric substrate materials, and designing electromagnetic band-gap (EBG) structure to isolate the RFID tag antenna from the effects of metallic back plane <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>. Usually, these design techniques increase the size of the tag or achieve a rigid structure. The bulk and rigid on metal RFID tags often limit their use on various shaped objects.</p><p>This letter is in continuation of an earlier work, presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>, where the fabrication technique of the high-dielectric flexible substrate for an RFID tag antenna and its performance is presented. However, in this letter, a new small single-conductor-layer tag is developed for multiplatform metal mountable applications. The proposed tag is composed of a small tag antenna and a thin custom-made flexible composite substrate. The antenna (14×28 mm<sup>2</sup>) is patterned out of copper tape and attached to the flexible substrate disk (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 5.649em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.048em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.99em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-3"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-4"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-5"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-6"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-7" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">radius</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-8" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-9" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">16</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">{\hbox{radius}} = 16</script></tex-math></inline-formula>mm, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-10" role="math" style="width: 7.39em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.67em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.61em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-11"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-12"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-13"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-14"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-15"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-16" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">thickness</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-17" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-18" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1.5</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">{\hbox{thickness}} = 1.5</script></tex-math></inline-formula>mm). The substrate material of the tag is a composite of BaTiO<sub>3</sub> and a polymer known as polydimethylsioxane (PDMS). BaTiO<sub>3</sub> is a high-dielectric ceramic in powder form, whereas polydimethylsiloxane in solid form is a flexible, transparent, and low-loss polymer material <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a>. The composite is a white, flexible, low-loss, and high-dielectric substrate material.</p><p>The proposed UHF RFID metal mountable tag antenna is flexible, thin, and small in size and has high read range and gain values with respect to its size and thickness. This type of flexible passive UHF RFID tag is suitable for several flat and cylindrical-shaped metallic objects.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Design</h2></div><p>The tag antenna is designed using HFSS ver.12. To demonstrate the performance of the tag antenna design, it is fabricated with a copper tape. The prototype tag is equipped with an NXP G2iL type of IC with sensitivity of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-19" role="math" style="width: 4.868em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.387em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1004.33em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-20"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-21"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-22" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-23"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-24"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-25" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-26" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-27" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-28" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">−</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-29" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">18</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">P_{\rm ic} = -18</script></tex-math></inline-formula>dBm. The impedance of the IC and the impedance model used to design the proposed tag are illustrated in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_2">[12]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_2">[13]</a>. The IC provided by the manufacturer comes with a strap attachment. The tag antenna fabricated using a copper tape is then attached on to a 1.5-mm-thick flexible polymer-ceramic composite substrate. The composite substrate has a small round disk structure with a radius of around 16 mm. The permittivity of the composite substrate is around 12 with a loss tangent less than or equal to 0.01. Detailed properties and fabrication technique have been stated in the previous work presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_2">[8]</a>, and a similar approach has been used in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_2">[14]</a>.</p><p>The dimension, geometry, and prototypes of the tag antenna are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>, whereas <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a> shows the mountable prototypes on cylindrical and flat objects.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6353124/6353124-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6353124/6353124-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>(a) Layout of the tag antenna structure. (b) Prototype of the tag.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6353124/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6353124/6353124-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6353124/6353124-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>(a) Mountable structures. <p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 1</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">2</a> show the layout and prototype of a symmetric dipole tag antenna structure. The IC is attached between the two feeding pads having dimensions “<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-30" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-31"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-32" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">a</script></tex-math></inline-formula>” and “<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-33" role="math" style="width: 0.483em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-34"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-35" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">b</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">b</script></tex-math></inline-formula>,” with conductive epoxy. The gap between the two “<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-36" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-37"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-38" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">a</script></tex-math></inline-formula>” edges is equal to 2 mm. The two halves of the dipole structures are shorted or T-matched along the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-39" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-40"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-41" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-7">y</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-axis with the help of a line “<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-42" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-8">f</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.” The T-matching network works as an impedance transformer and hence helps in reducing the overall size of the proposed tag antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_2">[15]</a>. Introducing 1-mm-thick slots (“<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-45" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-46"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-47" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-9">g</script></tex-math></inline-formula>”) in the two halves of the dipole structure further decreases the operating frequency of the tag antenna, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>. <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> lists the dimensions of the geometrical parameters of the tag, shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(a)</a>.

<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Simulation and Measurement Results</h2></div><p>This section demonstrates the performance of the metal mountable flexible UHF RFID tag antenna on a flat metallic plate and metallic cylinder. The results are supported with the simulation and measured results. The tag is measured in a compact anechoic chamber using a linearly polarized reader antenna connected to an RFID measurement system <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_3">[16]</a>.</p><p>To achieve the maximum performance of the tag, the antenna and the IC should be well matched to have a maximum power transfer between the antenna and the IC. The power reflection coefficient is the ratio of the incident power on the tag antenna <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-51" role="math" style="width: 2.766em; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-63" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-64" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">g</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-65" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; </p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6353124/6353124-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6353124/6353124-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>Measured and simulated read range of the metal mountable tag on flat metallic sheets of various sizes at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-325" role="math" style="width: 1.524em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.194em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.458em 1001.19em 2.517em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-326"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-327" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">+</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-328" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.163em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">+z</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-axis of the tag.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6353124/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>

top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-370"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-371"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-373"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-374"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-375"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-376"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-377" style="font-size: 70.7%; The regulated <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-380" role="math" style="width: 2.766em; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-384"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-385"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-386"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-387"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-388" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">E</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-389" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">I</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-390" style="font-size: 70.7%; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-395" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; This is the minimum continuous power required from the transmitter to turn on the tag IC and enable the tag to send a response back to the reader. To predict and verify the tag's performance on various metallic objects, the read ranges were simulated using the following equation: <disp-formula id="deqn4" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-400" role="math" style="width: 100%; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.2em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-467"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-468"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-469" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-26">P_{\rm ic}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the IC sensitivity and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-474" role="math" style="width: 1.264em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.14em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-475"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-476"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-477" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">G</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-478"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-479"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-480" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-27">G_{\rm r}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> represents the realized gain of the tag antenna. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 4</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">5</a> show the measured and simulated read ranges of the tag antenna on flat metallic sheets of different sizes and metallic cylinders of various radii, with a length of 120 mm.</p><p>From <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a> and <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a>, it can be observed that the performance (read range, realized gain, and efficiency) of the tag increases with the increase in the size of the metallic sheet. This can be due to the increase in directivity of the radiation pattern and the separation of the tag from the currents on the edges of the metallic surface. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a> and <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a> show that the tag wrapped over a smaller-radius cylinder has comparatively higher read range than on a cylinder with a larger radius. However, the change in the performance of the tag antenna is reduced as the radius of the cylinder increases. It is important to see from <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 4</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">5</a> that the tag operates on almost the same frequency band, regardless of the size and radius of the metallic surface.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a> shows the measured normalized gain radiation pattern mounted on flat and cylindrical metallic objects.

<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6353124/6353124-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6353124/6353124-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Amplitude of the surface current density on (a) a flat metallic surface (100×100 mm<sup>2</sup>) and (b) the tag antenna structure, accepting 100 mW of power.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6353124/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>, the E- (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-489" role="math" style="width: 1.084em; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-492" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">yz</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) and H- (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-493" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1001.02em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-494"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-495" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-496" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-31">xz</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) plane of the measured radiation pattern over flat and cylindrical metallic objects are shown. The radiation pattern of the tag becomes more directional with an increase in the flat surface of the metallic object on which it is mounted or wrapped. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 7</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">8</a> show the image current density on the conducting surface, generated due to the metal mounted tag antenna.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6353124/6353124-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6353124/6353124-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Amplitude of the surface current density on (a) a metallic cylinder (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-497" role="math" style="width: 6.022em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.765em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1004.7em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-498"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-499"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-500"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-501"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-502"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-503" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">radius</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-504" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">{\hbox{radius}} = 25</script></tex-math></inline-formula>mm) and (b) the tag antenna structure, accepting 100 mW of power.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6353124/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>It can be seen from <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 7</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">8</a> that the highest amplitude of the surface current density is concentrated around the T-matching of the antenna. The flexible high-dielectric substrate material helps to decrease the image current density on the conductive surface by increasing the isolation between the antenna and the mounted surface. <a ref-type="table" anchor="table3" class="fulltext-link">Table III</a> shows a comparison of the proposed metal mountable tag antenna with some state-of-the-art metal mountable RFID tag antenna designs. To have a fair comparison of the read ranges (Est. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-506" role="math" style="width: 1.745em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-507"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-508"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-509" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.465em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.47em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-528"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-529"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.465em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-530" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-531"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-532"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-533" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">E</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-534" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">I</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-535" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-536" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">P</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">P_{\rm EIRP}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> values equal to 3.28 W. According to <a ref-type="table" anchor="table3" class="fulltext-link">Table III</a>, the proposed tag has competitive results with a thin, small, single conducting layer and flexible and multiplatform metal mountable structure.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table3"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table III </b>Comparison of the Proposed Tag to Some State-of-the-Art Designs<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6353124/6353124-table-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6353124/6353124-table-3-small.gif" alt="Table III" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p><p>The proposed metal mountable flexible UHF RFID tag antenna shows a good performance with respect to its size and thickness. The read range, realized gain, and efficiency increase with the increase in the size of the metallic plate. The high-permittivity and low-loss flexible substrate enables to achieve a smaller tag antenna design with high performance.</p><p>In addition to aforementioned properties, the nature of the composite substrate makes it less vulnerable to breakings, heat, humidity, and other damaging effects. These features will be further analyzed as part of the future work by utilizing various inkjet printing and embedding techniques to print and embed the tag antenna inside the composite substrate material.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>A small flexible metal mountable UHF RFID tag is designed and fabricated on a polymer-ceramic substrate material. The high-permittivity flexible composite substrate helps in reducing the size of the tag antenna and increases the isolation between the antenna and the metallic object. The thin flexible structure of the tag allows it to be wrapped or placed on any cylindrical and flat metallic object. The results show that the designed multiplatform tag antenna has a high read range and gain with a small and thin tag structure.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>
